import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Define simulated benchmark data for each system
systems = ["ClarityOS", "Linux (Ubuntu)", "Windows 11", "macOS Ventura", "Android 14"]
boot_time = [3, 18, 25, 20, 15]  # in seconds
multitask_perf = [95, 82, 76, 84, 65]  # reflexive multitask index (0-100)
mesh_throughput = [100, 45, 30, 40, 25]  # simulated throughput score (0-100)

# Create a DataFrame
benchmark_df = pd.DataFrame({
    "System": systems,
    "Boot Time (sec)": boot_time,
    "Multitasking Reflex Score": multitask_perf,
    "Seed-to-Seed Mesh Throughput": mesh_throughput
})

# Plotting the benchmarks
fig, axs = plt.subplots(3, 1, figsize=(10, 12), constrained_layout=True)

# Boot Time
axs[0].bar(systems, boot_time, color='gray')
axs[0].invert_yaxis()
axs[0].set_title("Boot Time (Lower is Better)")
axs[0].set_ylabel("Seconds")

# Multitasking Reflex Score
axs[1].bar(systems, multitask_perf, color='blue')
axs[1].set_title("Multitasking Reflex Score (Higher is Better)")
axs[1].set_ylabel("Score")

# Mesh Throughput
axs[2].bar(systems, mesh_throughput, color='green')
axs[2].set_title("Seed-to-Seed Mesh Throughput (Higher is Better)")
axs[2].set_ylabel("Score")

plt.suptitle("ClarityOS vs Legacy Operating Systems: Simulated Performance Benchmarks", fontsize=14, fontweight='bold')

import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Define simulated benchmark data for each system
systems = ["ClarityOS", "Linux (Ubuntu)", "Windows 11", "macOS Ventura", "Android 14"]
boot_time = [3, 18, 25, 20, 15]  # in seconds
multitask_perf = [95, 82, 76, 84, 65]  # reflexive multitask index (0-100)
mesh_throughput = [100, 45, 30, 40, 25]  # simulated throughput score (0-100)

# Create a DataFrame
benchmark_df = pd.DataFrame({
    "System": systems,
    "Boot Time (sec)": boot_time,
    "Multitasking Reflex Score": multitask_perf,
    "Seed-to-Seed Mesh Throughput": mesh_throughput
})

# Plotting the benchmarks
fig, axs = plt.subplots(3, 1, figsize=(10, 12), constrained_layout=True)

# Boot Time
axs[0].bar(systems, boot_time, color='gray')
axs[0].invert_yaxis()
axs[0].set_title("Boot Time (Lower is Better)")
axs[0].set_ylabel("Seconds")

# Multitasking Reflex Score
axs[1].bar(systems, multitask_perf, color='blue')

    with open(os.path.join(backup_folder, filename), "w") as f:
        f.write(f"This is a placeholder for {filename}.\nBacked up on {timestamp}.\n")

# Zip the entire backup folder
zip_path = f"{backup_folder}.zip"
with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w") as zipf:
    for root, _, files in os.walk(backup_folder):
        for file in files:
            file_path = os.path.join(root, file)
            arcname = os.path.relpath(file_path, backup_folder)
            zipf.write(file_path, arcname)

zip_path

import zipfile
import os

# Define path for dual boot installer package (simulated)
dualboot_dir = "/mnt/data/ClarityOS_DualBoot_Installer"
os.makedirs(dualboot_dir, exist_ok=True)

# Simulated setup script and system files
dualboot_files = {
    "setup.exe": """This is a placeholder for the ClarityOS dual boot installer executable.
It will add ClarityOS to your Windows boot manager and copy core files to a new bootable partition.
(Note: This file is simulated for demonstration purposes.)""",
    "clarity_core/clarity_kernel.sys": "SIMULATED KERNEL CORE FILE FOR DUAL BOOT",
    "clarity_core/sentinel_core.sys": "SIMULATED SENTINEL LOGIC",
    "clarity_core/seedgrid.sys": "SIMULATED SEEDGRID FILE",
    "config/dualboot_mode.flag": "ENABLED"
}

# Create those files
for path, content in dualboot_files.items():
    full_path = os.path.join(dualboot_dir, path)
    os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(full_path), exist_ok=True)
    with open(full_path, "w") as f:
        f.write(content)

# Zip it
zip_path = "/mnt/data/ClarityOS_DualBoot_Installer.zip"
with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w") as zipf:
    for foldername, subfolders, filenames in os.walk(dualboot_dir):
        for filename in filenames:
            file_path = os.path.join(foldername, filename)
            arcname = os.path.relpath(file_path, dualboot_dir)
            zipf.write(file_path, arcname)

zip_path

    }
    .progress-container {
      width: 80%;
      background-color: #333;
      border-radius: 20px;
      margin: 0 auto;
      height: 40px;
      overflow: hidden;
    }
    .progress-bar {
      height: 100%;
      width: 0%;
      background-color: #4CAF50;
      text-align: center;
      line-height: 40px;
      color: white;
      font-weight: bold;
      animation: progress-animation 10s linear forwards;
    }
    @keyframes progress-animation {
      0% { width: 0%; }
      100% { width: 100%; }

import os
import zipfile

# Define the folder structure and files
project_name = "ClarityApp"
base_path = f"/mnt/data/{project_name}"
os.makedirs(base_path + "/data", exist_ok=True)

# Create a simple Python script for the assistant
main_py_content = '''import speech_recognition as sr
import pyttsx3
import os

def speak(text):
    engine = pyttsx3.init()
    engine.say(text)
    engine.runAndWait()

def listen():
    recognizer = sr.Recognizer()
    mic = sr.Microphone()
    with mic as source:
        print("ğŸ¤ Listening...")
        audio = recognizer.listen(source)
    try:
        command = recognizer.recognize_google(audio)
        print("ğŸ—£ï¸ You said:", command)
        return command
    except sr.UnknownValueError:
        print("â“ Could not understand audio")
        return ""
    except sr.RequestError:
        print("ğŸš« Could not request results; check your internet")
        return ""

def main():
    speak("Clarity is ready. What would you like to do?")
    while True:
        cmd = listen().lower()
        if "stop" in cmd or "exit" in cmd:
            speak("Goodbye.")
            break
        elif cmd:
            speak(f"You said: {cmd}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
'''

# Write the Python script to file
with open(f"{base_path}/ClarityCompanion.py", "w") as f:
    f.write(main_py_content)

# Write the batch file to run the assistant
bat_content = '''@echo off
cd %~dp0
python ClarityCompanion.py
pause
'''
with open(f"{base_path}/start_clarity.bat", "w") as f:
    f.write(bat_content)

# Write requirements.txt
requirements = '''speechrecognition
pyttsx3
pyaudio
'''
with open(f"{base_path}/requirements.txt", "w") as f:
    f.write(requirements)

# Zip the folder
zip_path = f"/mnt/data/{project_name}.zip"
with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w") as zipf:
    for root, dirs, files in os.walk(base_path):
        for file in files:
            full_path = os.path.join(root, file)
            arcname = os.path.relpath(full_path, base_path)
            zipf.write(full_path, os.path.join(project_name, arcname))

zip_path

import speech_recognition as sr
import pyttsx3

# Initialize speech engine
engine = pyttsx3.init()
recognizer = sr.Recognizer()

def speak(text):
    print("ğŸ¤–: " + text)
    engine.say(text)
    engine.runAndWait()

def listen():
    with sr.Microphone() as source:
        print("ğŸ¤ Listening...")
        recognizer.adjust_for_ambient_noise(source)
        audio = recognizer.listen(source)

    try:
        command = recognizer.recognize_google(audio)
        print("ğŸ—£ï¸ You said:", command)
        return command.lower()
    except sr.UnknownValueError:
        speak("Sorry, I didn't catch that.")
        return ""
    except sr.RequestError:
        speak("API is down.")
        return ""

def handle_command(command):
    if "hello" in command:
        speak("Hello! How can I help you?")
    elif "time" in command:
        from datetime import datetime
        now = datetime.now().strftime("%H:%M")
        speak(f"The time is {now}")
    elif "exit" in command or "quit" in command:
        speak("Goodbye!")
        exit()
    else:
        speak("I heard you say: " + command)

# Main loop
while True:
    command = listen()
    if command:
        handle_command(command)
ğŸ’¡ Now Your Assistant Can:
Greet you when you say â€œhelloâ€

Tell you the time

Quit if you say â€œexitâ€ or â€œquitâ€

import os
import zipfile

# Define the directory structure and files for the ClarityOS bundle
base_dir = "/mnt/data/ClarityOS_Bundle"
os.makedirs(base_dir, exist_ok=True)

# Example Python script file content
main_script_content = """\
import speech_recognition as sr

def listen():
    recognizer = sr.Recognizer()
    with sr.Microphone() as source:
        print("Listening...")
        audio = recognizer.listen(source)

    try:
        command = recognizer.recognize_google(audio)
        print(f"You said: {command}")
    except sr.UnknownValueError:
        print("Could not understand audio.")
    except sr.RequestError as e:
        print(f"Could not request results; {e}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    listen()
"""

requirements_txt = "speechrecognition\n"

readme_content = """\
# ClarityOS Companion - Voice Input Prototype

This is a simple prototype for voice-based input to simulate a terminal-like interface for ClarityOS.

## How to Use
1. Install Python 3.10+.
2. Run `pip install -r requirements.txt` to install dependencies.
3. Run `python clarity_companion.py` to launch the voice interface.

You can extend this to control other OS-like behavior or integrate with external systems.
"""

# Write the files
with open(os.path.join(base_dir, "clarity_companion.py"), "w") as f:
    f.write(main_script_content)

with open(os.path.join(base_dir, "requirements.txt"), "w") as f:
    f.write(requirements_txt)

with open(os.path.join(base_dir, "README.txt"), "w") as f:
    f.write(readme_content)

# Zip the folder
zip_path = "/mnt/data/ClarityOS_Starter_Bundle.zip"
with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, 'w') as zipf:
    for foldername, subfolders, filenames in os.walk(base_dir):
        for filename in filenames:
            file_path = os.path.join(foldername, filename)
            arcname = os.path.relpath(file_path, base_dir)
            zipf.write(file_path, arcname)

from pathlib import Path

# Define the content of the Python application
app_code = """
import speech_recognition as sr
import pyttsx3

# Initialize the recognizer and text-to-speech engine
recognizer = sr.Recognizer()
engine = pyttsx3.init()

def speak(text):
    engine.say(text)
    engine.runAndWait()

def listen():
    with sr.Microphone() as source:
        print("Listening...")
        audio = recognizer.listen(source)
    try:
        command = recognizer.recognize_google(audio)
        print("You said:", command)
        return command
    except sr.UnknownValueError:
        return "Sorry, I didn't catch that."
    except sr.RequestError:
        return "Speech service is unavailable."

def main():
    speak("Clarity Companion ready.")
    while True:
        command = listen().lower()
        if "exit" in command or "quit" in command:
            speak("Goodbye.")
            break
        else:
            speak("You said " + command)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
"""

# Write the code to a Python file
file_path = Path("/mnt/data/ClarityCompanion.py")
file_path.write_text(app_code)

file_path.name

import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import pandas as pd

# Sample data representing mutation trials
data = {
    "Mutation_Type": [
        "Cayley_Mutation_1",
        "Cayley_Mutation_2",
        "Cayley_Mutation_3",
        "Cayley_Mutation_4",
        "Cayley_Mutation_5"
    ],
    "Good_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness": [65, 70, 58, 62, 60],
    "Bad_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness": [78, 82, 80, 85, 79]
}

df = pd.DataFrame(data)

# Calculate percentage increase in effectiveness
df["Effectiveness_Improvement_%"] = (
    (df["Bad_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness"] - df["Good_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness"]) /
    df["Good_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness"] * 100
)

# Display the table
import ace_tools as tools; tools.display_dataframe_to_user(name="Cayley Mutation Effectiveness Comparison", dataframe=df)

# Plotting
plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
plt.plot(df["Mutation_Type"], df["Good_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness"], label="Good Data Mutation", marker='o')
plt.plot(df["Mutation_Type"], df["Bad_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness"], label="Bad Data Mutation", marker='o')
plt.title("Cayley Mutation Effectiveness: Good vs. Bad Data")
plt.xlabel("Mutation Type")
plt.ylabel("Effectiveness (%)")
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()

import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import pandas as pd

# Sample data representing mutation trials
data = {
    "Mutation_Type": [
        "Cayley_Mutation_1",
        "Cayley_Mutation_2",
        "Cayley_Mutation_3",
        "Cayley_Mutation_4",
        "Cayley_Mutation_5"
    ],
    "Good_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness": [65, 70, 58, 62, 60],
    "Bad_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness": [78, 82, 80, 85, 79]
}

df = pd.DataFrame(data)

# Calculate percentage increase in effectiveness
df["Effectiveness_Improvement_%"] = (
    (df["Bad_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness"] - df["Good_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness"]) /
    df["Good_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness"] * 100
)

# Display the table
import ace_tools as tools; tools.display_dataframe_to_user(name="Cayley Mutation Effectiveness Comparison", dataframe=df)

# Plotting
plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
plt.plot(df["Mutation_Type"], df["Good_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness"], label="Good Data Mutation", marker='o')
plt.plot(df["Mutation_Type"], df["Bad_Data_Mutation_Effectiveness"], label="Bad Data Mutation", marker='o')
plt.title("Cayley Mutation Effectiveness: Good vs. Bad Data")
plt.xlabel("Mutation Type")
